Last Week's Bond Prices Showed Drastic Fluctuations

Price increases and decreases were both suspended from trading, and the results varied.

Trading was suspended on the weekend in preparation for settlement.

During the past week (from December 21st to 26th), although spot prices for various bonds on the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange were still quoted, the volume of transactions was lower than before. Over the four days, a total of 100,850 yuan worth of transactions took place, including approximately 18,000 yuan of the 20th-year Customs Salt Tax bonds, 13,000 yuan of the 19th-year Customs bonds, and 10,000 yuan each of the demobilization and reorganization 20th-year bonds. The remaining bonds each accounted for approximately 7,000 to 8,000 yuan. Although the futures market was approaching settlement, trading was suspended on the weekend in preparation for the settlement of December futures. However, the minimum price limit for bonds previously set by the Ministry of Finance was lifted on Monday, and market buyers and sellers were once again free to trade. Market prices fluctuated significantly, and transaction volume increased. Market sentiment was active. The total volume of transactions was 6,780,000 yuan for each of the first two days of the week, 9,600,000 yuan on Wednesday, and nearly 12,000,000 yuan on Thursday. The total transaction volume for the four days was 25,200,050 yuan, an increase of over 3,000,000 yuan compared to the previous week. This included 2,705,000 yuan for the December Unified Tax futures, 3,090,000 yuan for the January futures, 2,530,000 yuan for the December 10th-year Customs futures, 2,835,000 yuan for the January futures, 2,020,000 yuan for the December Salt Tax futures, 2,750,000 yuan for the January futures, 1,710,000 yuan for the December 19th-year Customs futures, 1,370,000 yuan for the January futures, 1,925,000 yuan for the December 19th-year Philanthropy futures, 2,160,000 yuan for the January futures, 1,635,000 yuan for the December 20th-year bonds, 1,955,000 yuan for the January futures, 2,370,000 yuan for the December Demobilization bonds, 690,000 yuan for the January futures, 1,420,000 yuan for the December Reorganization bonds, and 105,000 yuan for the January futures. Remaining amounts included 340,000 yuan for the December Customs Tax futures, 75,000 yuan for the January futures, 615,000 yuan for the December Six Percent bonds, 110,000 yuan for the January futures, 420,000 yuan for the December 1996 Public Bonds, and 165,000 yuan for the January futures. As for the trend of public bond prices during the past week, during the first two days of the week, the minimum price limit for bonds had just been lifted, and the diplomatic situation became increasingly serious. The Japanese army was advancing on Jinzhou on a large scale, and there were widespread concerns that formal war was inevitable. In addition, there were rumors that the principal and interest of certain bonds would be postponed due to financial difficulties. As a result, market sentiment was very uneasy for a time, and the market was extremely tense. If there were problems with the principal and interest of the bonds, the financial industry would be severely affected. Therefore, the panic in the market was unprecedented since the price declines. Selling pressure was very strong, and on Monday, prices fell sharply by around 3 yuan. Trading in the current month's Unified Salt Tax futures was even suspended due to rumors. The downward trend continued on Tuesday, with further small declines of 1 to 2 yuan. On Wednesday, market sentiment was still very weak, and bond prices continued to reach new lows. However, in the afternoon, market sentiment improved slightly, and the situation improved somewhat. Buying interest was strong, and bond prices mostly rebounded. Although many bond prices fell sharply, the 19th-year Philanthropy bonds rose by nearly 2 yuan, and the 20th-year Customs and Salt Tax bonds also rebounded by several jiao. Although the situation in Northeast China remained severe on Thursday, the bond market environment had become more optimistic. The previous rumors of postponed payments of bond principal and interest proved to be untrue, and the principal and interest of bonds due this month had been paid. Market sentiment was greatly relieved, and buying interest was very strong. For a time, the market became a short squeeze, and prices rose sharply. Eight bonds were suspended from trading after rising to the limit price, and many others rose by around 3 yuan. However, the results were mixed. The 19th-year Philanthropy, Six Percent bonds, and Reorganization bonds rose slightly, while the others fell slightly. Judging from the bond market situation, it is not yet permissible to be optimistic. How to encourage investment and bring about a better future is the responsibility of both the government and the financial industry. The current situation is still very concerning, it is said. Last Week's Yarn Sales: Sichuan Merchants Exclusively Prosperous

Negotiated transactions were bleak.

The yarn market weakened during the past week, mainly due to the country's multiple difficulties. The Japanese army's harassment in Jinzhou intensified daily, Sino-Japanese relations became increasingly precarious, financial conditions tightened daily, and market sentiment became more panicked. As a result, the market became sluggish and depressed. Nowadays, there is an increasing number of Japanese yarns changing brands and being packaged in foreign locations, which has dealt a major blow to the sales of domestic yarns. However, Sichuan merchants still have a strong interest in domestic yarns, and because their inventories in Sichuan are low, they are very interested in making large-scale purchases. Unfortunately, tight credit conditions and the lack of external trade in Sichuan have prevented them from doing so as desired. Nevertheless, they have purchased approximately 12,000 bales of domestic yarn in total. Other merchants have rarely taken action. The inactivity in negotiated transactions is due to the chaotic situation and the approaching end of the year, as businesses prepare to close and are unable to act freely. The selling prices of current yarns are also declining daily, it is said. The following is a comparative table of the highest and lowest prices of negotiated yarn for each month:

Last Week's Cotton Market Tight

The majority's attitude did not soften.

Factory demand remained unmoved.

The cotton market was quite soft at the beginning of the week due to the sluggishness of the foreign cotton market. The combined price of American cotton was between 25 and 28 taels. All factories were stocked full of foreign cotton, and there was no need for domestic cotton. Therefore, although the supply of domestic cotton was low, factory demand stagnated. In addition, shipments from the Hankou route were increasing. Everyone agreed that the market was weak, but the majority of merchants and those from Hankou had very small stakes and were keen on going long, so they did not soften their stance. The last day of this month was the settlement date. Merchants from Ningbo were receiving goods and settling Yao flower contracts, which caused the standard market price to suddenly rise by 5 qian. Forward contracts were also pulled up. As a result, the prices for each month were up 5 qian for the near month and 1 to 2 qian for the distant months compared to the previous week. The price of American cotton rose by 20 pounds, it is said. The following is a comparative table of the highest and lowest prices of Hankou cotton for each month:

Grain Market Rice Prices on the Lower Reaches of the River Slightly Firm

Southern cargo: Yesterday, about 20 boats carrying goods from Changzhou, Wuxi, Xianzi, and other regions arrived. Merchants refused to sell unless prices increased. Furthermore, prices in production areas such as Songjiang and Qingpu were 30 to 40 jiao lower than prices in Shanghai. Dealers took advantage of favorable weather conditions and increased activity. Thick new japonica rice and early and late indica rice prices increased by nearly a jiao. Rice affected by rain had a weak market and prices softened slightly.

New Gate: Not many ships arrived. West Road white japonica rice was actively sold in the city market, and prices increased by about a jiao. Merchants from rural villages purchased 2,000 bales of thin early indica rice, and prices increased by 2 to 3 jiao. Du Yangjian and Bu Jian rice were firm. There were few arrivals of rain-affected glutinous rice, and sales to cake shops were active. The market trend was mediocre.

Sugar Market: Raw Sugar and White Sugar Gradually Rise

Hechi (Dutch raw sugar) quotations opened up five fen.

Yesterday, there were no telegrams from sugar production areas due to the weekend. There were few transactions on the association's market quotations. Number 24 Dutch sugar was in short supply and was quoted at a surprisingly high price. Initially, there was some resistance, but buyers were quite active. The opening transaction price was 9 taels and 6 qian and a half. Sellers continued to raise prices, and later it rose to 9 taels and 7 qian. The market trend stabilized somewhat. Mian He (soft Dutch sugar) was at 11 taels and 3 qian, Number 20 medium white sugar was at 9 taels and 6 qian, Number 8 Hechi was at 8 taels and 3 qian and a half, and Number 9 rose to 8 taels and 6 qian. The market trend was strong. Transactions of Taikoo sugar were more sluggish. B Mark was at 11 taels 7 qian and a half to 7 fen and a half, and HX Mark was at 11 taels and 5 qian and a half. The trend was stable. The quotation from Hua Xin was that PN Mark Hechi current goods were sold for several hundred bags at a price of 8 taels and 6 qian per yuan, which was an increase of 5 fen compared to the previous quotation, and the market sentiment was strong, with a large trend of gradual price increases, it is said.

Hardware: Thin Galvanized Iron Sheet Sales Flowing Smoothly

Recently, the arrival of thin English galvanized iron sheets has been very abundant, and there is a concern about the market being overstocked. However, sales have been extremely smooth in recent days. Merchants from the Yangtze River region are buying as much as possible, and merchants from inland regions are also actively purchasing. Merchants from Fuzhou, Longkou, Tianjin, and other regions are also inquiring. Therefore, in this sluggish market, it can be said that it is unique in terms of transaction volume. As a result, the standard price has been maintained and has not fallen. The current market price is 1 tael and 4 qian per sheet for 7 feet and 1 tael and 1 qian and a half per sheet for 6 feet. Although yesterday was Sunday, there were still as many as 7,000 to 8,000 sheets transacted. Considering the recent optimistic sentiment, it is feared that the standard price will not fall in the future, it is said.

Sun Ke and Others Accompanied Guangdong Committee Members to Beijing Yesterday

However, Wang Jingwei and Zhang Fakui remained in Shanghai.

Central Committee members Sun Ke and Li Wenfan, who had a dispute at the second meeting of the Fourth Central Committee, withdrew from the meeting and came to Shanghai. The conference sent representatives Jiang Zuobin, Chen Mingshu, and Zou Lu to Shanghai one after another to explain and persuade them. Sun and others agreed to enter Beijing the night before. However, Sun intended to travel with Wang Jingwei. Therefore, before leaving yesterday, he went to the hospital with Zou Lu and Chen Mingshu at 10:30 a.m. to meet Wang and strongly urged him to accompany them. Wang immediately agreed to go to Beijing within the next few days. Sun and others then returned to Beijing with Guangdong Committee members Li Jishen and Li Zongren at 3:30 p.m. to attend the Central Committee meeting. Yesterday, Li Jishen expressed his opinion to the Central Committee, advocating for the expansion of civil rights, the reorganization of people's organizations, and the addition of elected members to the Supervisory and Legislative Yuan. The following is a record of the various news obtained yesterday:

Sun and others urge Wang: Chen Mingshu and Zou Lu arrived in Shanghai the night before and visited Sun Ke around 9:00 p.m. with a joint letter from Lin Sen and others. Sun also understood and agreed to go to Beijing the next day. However, Sun intended to travel with Wang Jingwei. Therefore, Chen and Zou visited Sun again around 10:00 a.m. yesterday and then took Sun's car to the hospital at 10:30 a.m. to urge Wang. Wang, who was still recovering from his illness, did not agree to go with them but promised to go to Beijing within two or three days. Sun and others then returned to their residence at 11:30 a.m.

Accompanied Guangdong Committee members to Beijing: Since Wang would postpone his trip to Beijing, Sun and Li Wenfan decided to travel to the capital first at 3:15 p.m. with Guangdong Committee members Li Jishen and others. Upon hearing this, the Railway Bureau specially prepared a train with two decorated cars for the committee members to ride in. Around 3:10 p.m., Sun and others sent Jian Youwen in the car first. Photograph of Li Jishen and Li Zongren from the Guangdong Committee traveling to Beijing (taken by this newspaper).

Li Jishen, Li Wenfan, Zhang Huichang, Chen Mingshu, Chen Ce, Chen Qingyun, Zhan Juci, Zou Lu, Sun Ke, Huang Shaoxiong, and others arrived at the station one after another and immediately boarded the train. Li Zongren arrived late at 3:30 p.m., and the train did not depart until 3:35 p.m. In addition, Central Committee members Zeng Zhongming, Secretary Chen Jianru, Zhong Tianxin, and others also left Shanghai on the same train yesterday. However, Zhang Fakui remained in Shanghai and did not travel.

Li Jishen's proposals: Yesterday, Guangdong Committee member Li Jishen told people that he advocated for the expansion of civil rights, the addition of two-thirds elected members to the Supervisory and Legislative Yuan, and the reorganization of people's organizations to make them more united and solid. Only then would there be a way to handle all internal matters and only then would there be strength externally, it is said.

The County Party Committee Issued Two Telegrams Yesterday

Eliminate prejudices and jointly resist foreign aggression.

The Shanghai County Party Committee sent two telegrams to the Fourth Central Committee yesterday, one requesting that military officers be prevented from leaving their posts on the grounds of illness, and the other requesting the elimination of prejudices and joint resistance against foreign aggression. The original telegrams are recorded below. The first one: (Omitted above) Since the violent Japanese army occupied the Northeast and invaded the three provinces, we have felt that they are stronger and more barbaric than bandits. However, they still feel that their policies are too weak, so they have reorganized the cabinet and formed a cabinet under Inukai Tsuyoshi, the president of the Seiyukai, to implement the Tanaka Doctrine and implement a strong foreign policy. The attack on Jinzhou has become a reality, and the defenses in Guanzhong are urgent. At this time, it is appropriate to send more troops to defend the area in order to preserve the remaining territory and plan to recover the lost three provinces. However, it is reported that Rong Zhen has left Jinzhou on the grounds of illness and gone to Ping for medical treatment, treating national defense as a game and placing military duties outside of his concerns, going against the tide and not knowing what his conscience is. Currently, there is no one sitting in Jinzhou, and the defenses are empty. Once the Japanese attack, Jinzhou may fall again. Therefore, we especially telegraph to your committee to stop him as soon as possible, and quickly send troops to defend Jinzhou to resist foreign aggression. The people of the country are anxiously awaiting orders. The second one: (Omitted above) At this time, the invaders are getting deeper and deeper, and national destruction is imminent. All of us comrades should abandon prejudices and unite as one. There is no need to talk about political systems. We should immediately plan the major strategy of resisting foreign aggression. However, since September 18th, the country has been in turmoil for several months, and no one knows what to do. There have been disputes at the Shanghai meeting and competition in the elections. Fortunately, the Central Committee meeting has opened, and we can unite to deal with Japan. However, news has come that some members of the Central Committee have been absent due to illness and others have walked out in anger. The country is in difficulty, and there are many things to manage. Those who bear the responsibility of party affairs should be humble, tolerant, and willing to do their best to realize their responsibilities and overcome the difficulties of the country and turn danger into safety. They must not be willful and disregard the current crisis, which will only make the future of the nation more and more devastated. This committee is compelled to send this telegram in desperation, hoping to make a final struggle to support this dangerous situation. All members of the Central Committee should gather in the capital and not take independent action until a solution is reached. We are anxiously awaiting this.

Zhejiang National Salvation Association Promotion Association Holds Meeting Yesterday

The Zhejiang Provincial National Salvation Conference Promotion Association held its inaugural meeting yesterday (27th) at 1:00 p.m., with over 1,200 people in attendance. The temporary chairman was Ding Jimei. The meeting was held as scheduled. The presidium consisted of seven people: Chu Fucheng, Cha Renwei, Ding Jimei, Chen Anshu, Zhu Shaoqing, Liang Fucheng, and Ji Shiyuan. Chu Fucheng reported on the purpose of the meeting, and Liang Fucheng reported on the preparations for the association. The nine articles of the organizational outline were discussed, revised, and passed, and a declaration was issued. Twelve proposals were resolved: (1) Telegram to the Fourth Central Committee, requesting that Mr. Wang Jingwei and others' proposals be passed as soon as possible, the organizational law of the National Salvation Conference be promulgated, and the date of the conference be determined; (2) Circular telegram to all counties in Zhejiang, urging them to quickly organize a National Salvation Conference Promotion Association and unanimously demand that the conference be held as soon as possible; (3) Circular telegram to all counties, urging them to quickly organize volunteer armies, intensify training, and prepare for the war of resistance against Japan; (4) Telegram to the central government requesting that the senior officials who lost territory be punished; (5) Telegram to Ma Zhanshan requesting him to unite with friendly forces to counterattack; (6) Telegram to the central government requesting that 100,000 elite troops be quickly dispatched and led by Zhang Fakui to the north, and that all armies in the country that have volunteered to resist Japan be allowed to depart to recover the lost territories; (7) Opposition to military personnel holding political power; (8) Telegram to the central government requesting an investigation into the Nanjing 1217 tragedy, the strict punishment of the perpetrators, and the compensation of the injured and dead, and a guarantee that patriotic movements will not be destroyed again in the future. In addition, there were two temporary motions that were unanimously passed by the audience. Then, in accordance with the organizational outline, 31 executive committee members were elected to form the executive committee. Those elected were Chu Fucheng, Zhu Shaoqing, Yin Ruzhen, Dai Ren, Hu Fu, Ding Jimei, Cha Renwei, Gu Changzhen, Xu Zhi, Chen Anshu, Wang Baichun, Li Ganhao, Liang Fucheng, and others. The meeting then adjourned with slogans.

Lawyers Association Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committees

The Ninety-Sixth Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 96th joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members at its meeting place at the intersection of Route Belles and Route Lafayette in the French Concession yesterday (Sunday) at 11:00 AM. Committee members present included Liu Zuwang, Li Shirui, Shan Yuhua, Zhang Feixiong, Huang Han, Zhao Zuwei, Cai Nipei, Zhao Yuhuang, Yu Zhongluo, Shen Junru, Lu Shaozong, and others. Li Shirui was publicly elected as chairman, and Dai Jixian recorded the proceedings. The usual formalities were observed. The proposed resolutions are recorded below:

(1) A letter from the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government, forwarding a compilation of international treaties, regarding the compilation of treaties concerning relations between China and Japan in the Three Eastern Provinces, which is being rushed to print. Resolution: File for reference.

(2) The Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, acting on orders, is forwarding proposed revisions to the criminal law and criminal procedure law from the Legislative Yuan and soliciting opinions within two months for consideration and adoption. Resolution: Forward the original order to all members for review. If there are any opinions, report them to the association within one month for submission to the committee for review and compilation. A special committee will be formed, including all executive and supervisory committee members of this association as ex officio members, plus the addition of Guo Heng, Zhao Chen, Dong Kang, Wu Jingxiong, Zhang Yaozeng, Peng Qi, Sheng Zhenwei, Qiu Fenling, Liu Shifang, Qu Yue, Shen Yuesheng, Zhong Hongsheng, and others as special committee members.

(3) A letter from member Yang Changchi, responding to the case of Wang Xingsheng attacking and accepting a commission from the opposing party. Resolution: Forward to the original reporter for review.

(4) A letter from member Fei Guoxi, responding to the case of Jiang Yixian suing for incomplete handover of accounts. Resolution: Forward to the original reporter for review.

(5) The military group has selected Type A training dummy rifles, costing seven yuan each, and proposes to purchase two dozen initially. Request for approval. Resolution: Approved.

(6) The military group has hired a coach, with a monthly transportation allowance of twenty yuan. Request for retroactive approval. Resolution: Approved.

(7) A letter from the clerk's office of the Shanghai Special District Local Court, notifying that court translators should be restricted from practicing law within the same area of jurisdiction. Resolution: Members Jiang Chiping and Deng Jiabing were former translators at the First Special District Court. They should be notified, and the First Special District Court should be informed to notify us of any other translators who are currently practicing law.

(8) A temporary motion by committee member Shan Yuhua, requesting an interpretation of Article 8 of the new agreement for the Shanghai International Settlement Court, regarding whether the Shanghai Municipal Council's participation in lawsuits includes criminal cases. Resolution: Send a letter to the Second Higher Court Branch, forwarding it to a committee authorized to interpret the agreement for interpretation.

(9) A temporary motion by committee member Lu Shaozong, requesting an interpretation of the Criminal Procedure Law regarding cases where a self-prosecutor cannot be summoned for the second instance, and there is no remedial provision. How should such situations be handled? Request for interpretation. Resolution: Forward to the court, requesting an explanation. The original proposer will draft the document.

(10) Committee member Cai Nipei requests an explanation regarding a case where the High Court, for a case applying criminal law in the first instance, suddenly changed to the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits in the appellate judgment, thereby depriving the defendant of the right to appeal. A thorough examination of the provisions of the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits reveals no basis for changing the application in the appellate review, raising significant doubts. Resolution: Forward to the Judicial Yuan for interpretation. The original proposer will draft the document.

(11) Chairman Li Shirui proposed that, given the recent fragmentation of legal authority and the divergence of trials, it is imperative to find ways to rectify the harmful criminal law and other evil laws such as the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China and the continued implementation of the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits, causing the public to be wary. He proposes to promptly telegraph the Fourth First Plenary Session, requesting the convocation of a National Judicial Conference, the abolition of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic of China and the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits, and the abolition of special judicial organs outside the courts. Except for active-duty military personnel, no one should be subject to trial by any judicial organ other than a formal court. Resolution: Telegraph the Fourth First Plenary Session. The original proposer will draft the telegram.

(12) A temporary motion by committee member Zhang Feixiong, regarding the Shanghai Local Court's (1) refusal to accept the four types of legal forms printed by this association, (2) frequent delays in delivering judgments, and (3) failure to open court on time. Request to forward a letter for rectification. Resolution: Forward a letter to the Shanghai Local Court. The original proposer will draft the document, and the Standing Committee will review and issue it.

(13) A resolution from the previous meeting, regarding the declaration issued by this association, for submission to the association for review and issuance. Resolution: Passed.

(14) Applications for membership from lawyers Liu Chongzu, Shen Nianqu, Wang Yangshan, Huang Menggang, Gong Yi, Gou Shen, Chen Dingguo, Ji Dengyi, Cai Shaonian, Li Yiming, Hu Zhongjie, Liao Shigong, Li Yujun, Xu Tongxian, Huang Wenzao, Zhou Wenji, Liu Mengjing, Liu Jihan, Zhang [...]. Resolution: Passed.

The meeting was adjourned.

Japanese Army Determined to Attack Jinzhou

News of the Japanese army's attack on Jinzhou is becoming increasingly tense. Although the United Kingdom, the United States, and France have issued warnings to Japan, it is reported by those close to Japanese military personnel that the Japanese government is determined to attack Jinzhou, and it is inevitable. The attacking force consists of the First Division, originally stationed in Tokyo, and the Eighteenth Division, originally stationed in Korea, totaling approximately 20,000 men. They are ready to launch the attack. The original plan was to occupy Jinzhou by the end of this year, but now the aim is to occupy Jinzhou by early January of next year. A major war seems unavoidable. However, according to a certain diplomat, the Japanese army's attack on Jinzhou still depends on the attitude of the United States. The previous sudden order from the Japanese Emperor to withdraw troops from the attack on Jinzhou was indeed due to a statement by US Secretary of State Stimson. Therefore, if the United States expresses a strong stance in the future, the Japanese government may have some concerns.

Japanese Marines to Hold Large-Scale Exercises

Taking advantage of the Japanese army in Liaoshen attacking Jinzhou, the Japanese Marines stationed in Shanghai will hold a demonstration. Yesterday, Rear Admiral Shiozawa, commander of the unit, notified all Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai to hold joint naval exercises, scheduled for January 4 at the Japanese New Park in Hongkou.

Japan's Telecommunication Expenses to the League of Nations

Exceed 100,000 Yen

Yoshizawa Kenkichi, the Japanese ambassador to France who was newly appointed as Minister of Foreign Affairs, will soon return to Japan from Europe to take office. He first sent his son, Yoshizawa Hideo, back to Japan from France. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday aboard the Japanese ship Akikuni Maru. The Japanese Deputy Consul stationed in Shanghai, Mr. Iguchi, boarded the ship to greet him. According to Yoshizawa Hideo, the reason Japan was able to achieve victory in the League of Nations on the Manchurian issue was entirely due to effective propaganda. Because of the Manchurian issue, the cost of telecommunications used by the Japanese Embassy in France totaled over 100,000 yen. The French telegraph office gained a huge revenue from the Manchurian issue. His father, Yoshizawa Kenkichi, had lost several pounds due to the busyness of attending the League of Nations meeting. The Japanese spare no expense on international affairs, so our country's envoys cannot compete with them on the world stage.

Anti-Japanese Associations Everywhere Are Buying for Reference

Since the publication of the "Japanese Trademark Compilation" compiled by the International Commercial Research Institute, it is like having a demon-revealing mirror. Record of the Hubei Fellow-Provincials Association Relief Committee

Large Shipment of Cotton Clothes Transported to Hankou

The Hubei Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai's Emergency Relief Committee for Flood Disaster in Hubei Province held a committee meeting yesterday at its association office on Nan Wuxi Road. Du Xiangqing, Gao Jianqing, Li Yaoqin, Fan Wenhua, Sun Songnian, Lu Xingjie, Wang Hengqing, and over twenty others attended. Gao Jianqing was publicly elected as chairman. They reported a letter from the Hubei Flood Disaster Rehabilitation Committee and that there was still over 11,000 yuan remaining in the Shanghai Bank from the collected donations. Then, they discussed the proposed resolutions: (1) How should the relief funds currently in the bank be allocated? The majority believed that since the severe winter is approaching and the victims have no way to keep warm, and the price of cloth in Hankou is expensive, it would be better to entrust the Lianyi Charity Association to make 3,600 sets of men's and women's cotton clothes at 2.50 yuan per set, which was unanimously agreed upon. Du Xiangqing was instructed to contact the Lianyi Charity Association, and he immediately returned to report that it had been settled, and the association had also donated another 500 sets of cotton clothes. (2) How should the cotton clothes be packaged and transported after they are made? Resolved: A letter should be sent to the National Government's Flood Disaster Relief Committee, requesting them to ask the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Transportation to issue free transportation and tax-exempt passports. Liu [...], Chen and Peng Chunfang were appointed to supervise the packaging. (3) Can this association be concluded within the year? Resolved: Continue to urge the collection of donation ledgers. In any case, conclude it within the year. (4) Should the donors who have not been reported in the newspaper be supplemented? Resolved: When it is concluded, they will all be supplemented, and a credit record will be compiled and distributed for reporting. The meeting was adjourned. The association then received a reply letter from the National Government's Flood Disaster Relief Committee, stating: We have received your letter stating that you have raised 4,100 new winter clothes, totaling 102 packages, and plan to transport them to Hubei for distribution. Please apply for free transportation and tax-exempt passports, etc. The transportation of relief goods cannot be free of charge, but with a written certificate from the association, you can receive half-price discounts. Now, the association will issue a certificate for verification and send it to the China Merchants Bureau for contact. As for the tax-exempt passport, we have sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance for verification and issuance to the association. Please check and reply. It is also reported that the cotton clothes have been custom-cleared and transported to Hankou by the Zhengda Chenji Customs Brokerage Company free of charge.

Defense of the Fujian Aviation Patriotic Association

Refuting Rumors of Purchasing Aircraft and Transporting Soil

The Minnan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai received a telegram from the Fujian Aviation Patriotic Association yesterday (abridged title): A few months ago, Fujian fellow-provincials in Shanghai, based on reports from an unknown source, telegraphed the provincial government, requesting attention to the prohibition of Minnan soldiers from purchasing aircraft and transporting soil, etc. At that time, the association considered the wording to be (unclear code) and did not investigate who was being accused. Therefore, we just laughed it off and did not respond. Unexpectedly, recently we read in the newspaper that the rumors of purchasing aircraft and transporting soil are rampant. Fujian representatives Zheng Luosheng and others have proposed it to the Fourth National Congress, and the China Anti-Drug General Association has also listed it as an important agenda item, resolving to petition the government to severely investigate. For a time, fallacies spread, all alluding to this association. If this association remains silent and does not correct it, not only will the aviation effort fail, but the arguments will cause universal discouragement, which is enough to trap the country in a state of eternal destruction. At the beginning of this association's establishment, it clearly stated in Article 2 of its charter that this association uses civilian-run aviation power to prepare for the government's requisition of red eradication and national defense and is subject to the command and supervision of the central aviation supreme authority and local military authorities. Military actions should only handle matters, but not for any internal struggles. Since internal struggles are not provided, how can we provide people to transport soil? Furthermore, based on facts, let us assume that there is opium in Fujian, and it is planted everywhere. Then, those who force planting only need to levy taxes, so why purchase aircraft for transportation? Let us also assume that there is soil in Fujian, which is readily available. Then, the prohibition of opium is already very public, so there are many tools for transporting soil, such as the frequent occurrence of large-scale smuggling of opium cases in major trading ports, which is one example. Why use airplanes, which have a small capacity and many dangers? Let us further assume that aircraft can transport soil, but where will it be transported? May I ask whether it is possible for a foreign aircraft to fly and park arbitrarily in neighboring territories with different defense zones and neighboring countries with different nationalities? In short, planting opium is one thing, and aviation is another. The former has someone who can defend it, so this association does not need to overstep its bounds and speak for them. As for the latter, for the sake of following the late premier's teachings and for the sake of the reputation of aviation, this association dares to guarantee with the personality of all its members that such an unfilial act will not occur. If it does, we will willingly accept the extreme penalty and will not escape. It must be known that under the heavy oppression of foreign aggression and internal troubles, the cause of saving the country is not limited to aviation, but aviation is indeed the most important tool for saving the country. Since its establishment, this association has worked tirelessly and vigorously, and after many difficulties, it has achieved today's results. The ordered aircraft will arrive soon, and the facts will prove that the date is not far away. The gentlemen who made the proposal may as well wait a little longer before making a judgment. As for those who do not save the country considering those who save the country to be meddlesome, and empty talkers considering those who seek truth from facts to have hidden motives, they do not hesitate to fabricate evidence and conduct counter-propaganda, which only pleases the enemy and hurts our loved ones, cutting themselves off from the country without harming this association in the slightest. The members of this association will only strengthen their sincerity in carrying out the late premier's aviation teachings and, under the supervision and guidance of the military authorities, ensure that the Fujian Air Force emerges from itself and makes the most Zhou's application of pressure to the enemy. The impassioned words, I hope you will understand. The Fujian Aviation Patriotic Association kowtows.

British-Owned Public Bus Company Dismisses All Workers

Forced Operation with Police Protection Today

Company Prepares to Hire New Ticket Sellers

After the British-owned public bus workers went on strike due to work slowdowns, the company announced a deadline for the workers to return to work. As of yesterday, none had reported. The company immediately announced the dismissal of all workers and decided to operate routes 1, 9, and special express buses with police protection today. The details are as follows:

Strike Situation: After all ticket sellers of the British-owned public bus company went on strike, public buses on routes 1, 2, 4, 5, 6, 7, 9, 10, and special express cars AC were ordered to stop completely to avoid accidents. The general passengers felt very inconvenient. As for the striking workers, they gathered in the open space near the Jiaozhou Road racetrack yesterday morning to discuss countermeasures. It was reported that the result was a decision to use force to deal with those who violated strike discipline.

Dismissal of All: The company announced the day before yesterday, ordering all ticket sellers to report to the company for service yesterday, otherwise their jobs would be terminated, and they should return their uniforms and other items and collect their wages. As of yesterday from 5:00 AM to 6:00 PM, none of the 280+ ticket sellers reported. The manager then notified the writing room staff to settle the wages of all ticket sellers, announced the dismissal of all, and prepared to hire new workers. As for all drivers, ticket checkers, ticket writers, small workers, inspectors, etc., they did not join the ticket sellers' strike and still went to the company for service every morning and were scheduled as usual. However, because there was no one to sell tickets, they had no choice but to sign in and then leave. Wages were still paid by the company.

Company Losses: After all ticket sellers went on strike, the company had no choice but to stop the public buses on each route. It is reported that the daily loss due to the strike is about 4,000 yuan. As for the loss of wages for the striking ticket sellers, it is about 200+ yuan per day.

Protected Operation: To maintain traffic, the company agreed with the police station yesterday on measures to protect the operation of buses. The company decided to operate 14 buses on Route 1, from Jing'an Temple to Laobaizi Road, driven by Russians, with Chinese and Koreans checking tickets and acting as ticket sellers. Route 9 would have 20 buses, from Jing'an Temple to Tilanqiao, driven by Chinese, with Koreans checking tickets and Chinese checking tickets and writing tickets, acting as ticket sellers. Special express car A would have 3 buses, and special express car C would have 2 buses, driven by Chinese, with Western plainclothes ticket checkers acting as ticket sellers. The police station will devise ways to provide armed protection.

Japanese in Pudong Rihua Yarn Factory Refuse to Resume Work

Continued Unjustified Dismissal of 30 Workers

Arrested Female Workers Released by Court Yesterday

Japanese Use Marines to Intimidate Workers

After all the female workers in the cloth machine room of the Pudong Rihua Yarn Factory could not bear the oppression of the Japanese and went on strike, the Public Security Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau tried to persuade them to resume work. After a general meeting, it was resolved to obey the order with pain and resume work yesterday morning, but they were rejected by the Japanese, who used the Marines to intimidate the workers. They also continued to dismiss a large number of 40+ workers. Public sentiment was indignant, and the situation became serious again. The details are as follows:

General Meeting: At 5:00 PM on the 26th, the Rihua Branch Office of the Fifth District Cotton Spinning Workers' Union held a general meeting of all workers in the cloth machine room. Zheng Xiechen was publicly elected as chairman, and Sun Xiaoru recorded the minutes. The chairman reported on the Japanese capitalists' oppression of workers. Then, the discussion began and resolved: (1) The issue of workers resuming work. Resolved: To comply with the order, we will reluctantly enter the factory to resume work tomorrow. (2) If the Japanese resist the order and illegally refuse to resume work, all will vow to fight the Japanese capitalists to the end. (3) The case of Ni Jinxiu and Lu Xiaomei being falsely accused for no reason. Resolved: File a lawsuit with the court according to law. (4) The case of punishing the running dogs Hu Azhen and Zhang Fuying. Resolved: Permanently refuse to enter the factory. (5) If the factory increases work, deducts wages, and dismisses workers, we should unanimously refuse. Resolved: Passed. (6) Request the factory to give compensation for losses and retirement benefits. Resolved: In accordance with the Nanyang Tobacco Factory method, each person will receive a subsidy of six months. It did not end until 10:00 PM.

Refusal to Resume Work: All workers in the cloth machine room, in order to comply with the order, reluctantly entered the factory to resume work at 5:00 AM yesterday. The Japanese capitalists used a poisonous scheme, colluding with a few running dogs and Japanese thugs, to forcibly refuse them to enter the factory at the factory gate. As a result, more than 400 workers gathered in front of the factory gate until about 6:00 AM and had no choice but to return to the labor union to report the truth. The labor union immediately petitioned the party and government authorities to severely punish the Japanese who oppressed the workers.

Continued Oppression: After the Japanese refused all workers to resume work, they believed that Chinese workers could be deceived and resumed oppressive measures. Yesterday morning, they posted a notice at the factory gate, stating that Jiang Guiyuan and 30 other loyal old workers who had worked for many years would also be required to leave the workshop within ten days. Together with the previous cloth machine room, there were a total of 41 people, and other departments were not included. As for the 3,000+ workers in each department, they were also indignant due to the excessive oppression by the Japanese. They expressed deep sympathy for the cloth machine room and decided to assist them with their strength.

Release of Female Workers: After the female worker foreman Hu Azhen and the female worker Zhang Fuying, who colluded with the Japanese to act as accomplices, were beaten by all the female workers, they falsely reported to the police station, causing Lu Xiaomei, Ni Jinxiu, and other four people who had been wrongfully detained to be transferred to the local court. All workers petitioned, and Bao Cuidi and Cai Fuzhen, who had been innocently arrested, were released. Since the female worker foreman was not injured, Lu Xiaomei, Ni Jinxiu, and other two people were also released yesterday.

Intimidating Workers: Since the Rihua Yarn Factory was boycotted by our country, sales have stalled, and inventory has piled up, putting it in an unsustainable position. Therefore, it adopted an oppressive policy to take the opportunity to dismiss workers and not provide retirement benefits. This time, the workers could not bear the oppression and went on strike. The Japanese believed that their goal had been achieved. Now, seeing the workers resume work, they refused them and used the Japanese Marines to land and intimidate the resuming workers.

The Anti-Opium Society Bitterly Condemns the Failure to Enforce Opium Prohibition

Presents Nine Measures to the Central Conference

Advocating the Strict Enforcement of Opium Prohibition

In recent years, the scourge of opium has spread throughout the country, causing internal strife and planting the seeds of poverty and weakness, leading to widespread suffering and frequent foreign invasions. Tracing the root cause, this drug is the most severe culprit. In the 17th year of the Republic, the central government, upholding the teachings of the late Premier and responding to the demands of the people, revoked the powers of the Ministry of Finance and other departments to regulate opium prohibition, and established the Opium Prohibition Committee to handle the matter exclusively, demonstrating its intention to start anew with the people. However, regrettably, the government has neither the resolute determination to completely eradicate it nor the vigorous spirit to carry it out. Chen Tiaoyuan transported soil with justification, and his obstinacy went unpunished. Yang Shuzhuang was accused of smuggling, and Zhu Yu was sent to investigate. As a result, local officials regarded the prohibition laws as mere formalities and treated the decrees as straw dogs. When the Jiang'an soil case occurred in Shanghai, the military and police accused each other, revealing the truth. The people clearly understood who was responsible for transporting the soil and who was shielding the culprits. Unexpectedly, the central government's investigation resulted in the demotion of those investigating opium and the promotion of those shielding the soil. Such a reversal of right and wrong is astonishing. If there were no collusion between those above and below, how could such a phenomenon occur? The prohibition laws strictly prohibit the sale of soil and the levying of taxes, yet the Ministry of Finance openly established the Two Lakes Special Tax Bureau in Wuhan. The central government issued an order strictly prohibiting the cultivation of opium seedlings, yet the authorities in Anhui and Fujian forced the people to grow opium more severely than before. The people's appeals went unanswered. Recently, they have become even more brazen and are acting perversely. Those in charge are all central government officials, such as Chen Tiaoyuan and Hao Yuhua in Anhui, and Fang Shengtao, Zhang Zhen, Chen Guohui, and He Xianqi in Fujian. Their crimes are numerous, and public opinion is in an uproar, yet the central government has not shown any reaction. Furthermore, Fang Shengtao, the chief culprit in the opium cultivation in Fujian, was recently honored with the position of Central Committee member. The dignity of the party and the nation has been swept away. Such phenomena are intolerable to both party discipline and national law. If there is no change in course, the people of the whole country will not need the guns of the enemy; they will die under the policy of raising money by promoting drugs. At this critical moment, we must seek fundamental improvements in opium prohibition. Those who are concerned about the opium disaster in our country know that opium merchants, soil peddlers, hooligans, and ignorant people only create the fruit, while government officials and the army and navy in various places create the cause. Opium merchants and soil peddlers can only engage in small-scale drug trafficking, while military officers and officials, like tigers in a corner, blatantly engage in large-scale drug promotion plans that are hundreds or thousands of times larger. If we want to bring them to justice, they control the law. Therefore, officials and military officers who promote drugs for their own benefit are more guilty than soil peddlers and opium merchants. Expecting them to enforce opium prohibition is like asking a tiger for its skin. It is known that it is impossible. Therefore, in the future, attention should be paid to the selection and organization of personnel in opium prohibition agencies, and improvements should be made to ensure satisfactory results. Our association, with its responsibility for opposing drugs, has a clearer understanding and more accurate knowledge. Based on years of research, we present nine proposals for opium prohibition, hoping that the committee members of the conference will consider the difficulties of the party and the nation, the root causes of poverty and weakness, and accept and implement our proposals in full to eliminate this scourge, plan for prosperity for centuries, and save the country from collapse. Our association dares to represent the four hundred million people and sincerely pray. (1) For opium prohibition, the principle of Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug teachings, the provisions of the Kuomintang's party platform, and the unanimous demands of the people of the whole country should be upheld, and a policy of complete prohibition should be adopted, never to be changed. (2) Any form of opium monopoly and any method of using opium as tax revenue should be absolutely prohibited. Speech advocating opium monopoly should also be banned, and those who violate party discipline should be punished. (3) The special opium tax in the two lakes and Anhui, the public sale of opium paste in the two Guangdong provinces, and the planting of opium seedlings in Fujian, Anhui, and the northwest and southwest provinces, as well as the protection of private smuggling by the army and navy along the coast, are all open secrets that cannot be concealed. The transportation of soil by plane in Fujian is known far and wide, and the facts are all there. An immediate investigation of the responsible officials should be requested to maintain the prohibition laws. (4) The opium businesses in the concessions and leased territories, where unscrupulous foreigners use extraterritorial rights and consular jurisdiction to profit from drugs, as well as the prevalence of narcotics, should be studied by experts to find effective methods of prohibition. (5) The harm of opium and narcotics is extremely complex in various places. The relevant departments of the government should, together with people's organizations, form an investigation committee to conduct on-the-spot investigations using scientific methods to clarify the truth and establish the standards for prohibition. (6) The government should provide as much support and protection as possible for the people's anti-drug movement, such as eradicating opium seedlings, providing smoking cessation services, and conducting anti-drug education and publicity. It must also cooperate with the people's anti-drug organizations. Local party and government agencies that undermine the anti-drug movement should be punished. (7) The government should recognize opium prohibition as a major task for national salvation, and order officials at all levels to implement it strictly. All civil servants related to opium prohibition, such as county magistrates and public security bureau chiefs, should first join anti-drug organizations and swear to oppose drugs for life, demonstrating their determination to prohibit opium and facilitating public supervision. (8) The income from opium prohibition fines from judicial and public security agencies nationwide should be used to fund anti-drug education, publicity, and smoking cessation services, and should be jointly managed with people's organizations in accordance with Article 6 to achieve practical results. (9) The government should pay attention to the organization and personnel selection of opium prohibition agencies, prevent those who promote public sales and corruption from entering, maintain the strictness of the prohibition laws, and hold opium prohibition meetings regularly to receive public opinions.

Shareholders of the Tongsheng Money Exchange Accuse the Manager of Embezzlement

After the Tongsheng Money Exchange in this city closed on May 24th last year, a lawyer was appointed to liquidate the assets. Recently, shareholders Yang Jinrong, Yang Zhonghe, Yao Weiyong, and Zhang Xingchu discovered that the manager Zhang Chunlai had embezzled funds, and they hired lawyers Wu Linkun and Yuan Hanyun to file a criminal lawsuit with the First Special Court. The indictment stated that after Tongsheng's closure, Hu Yongde was entrusted to handle the liquidation and to publish advertisements to collect debts, but Hu Yongde's measures were improper and he did not report the defendant's fraud, resulting in no progress after several months of liquidation. The shareholders discovered the irregularities and managed to terminate the previous contract and hire another lawyer to liquidate the assets. Upon reviewing Tongsheng's books from the 19th year and the general ledger, it was discovered that Hu Yongde had privately transferred and cancelled numerous accounts receivable and payable since taking over the liquidation on May 27th, not only failing to uphold the principle of fair liquidation but also suspected of helping the defendant embezzle funds. One of the significant unlawful accounts discovered was a sum of 19,566.459 taels received from Zuyin Account, which was then paid to Chunyuan Account. Since Zuyin Account was a debtor of Tongsheng, the funds should have been properly stored for future distribution to creditors. However, the funds were paid to Chunyuan Account, which was clearly the defendant's account, as evidenced by Hu Yongde's "General Copy Book of Tongsheng Liquidation Office for the 20th Year of the Republic." Therefore, Hu Yongde's transfer of 19,566.459 taels was clearly transferring the funds received from Tongsheng's Zuyin Account into the defendant's hands, which is clearly an act of helping to conceal the crime. As the manager of Tongsheng, the defendant disregarded the shareholders' losses and intentionally embezzled funds at the time of Tongsheng's closure, which is a violation of conscience and a crime of professional embezzlement under Article 57, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Whether there was any other embezzlement will be investigated and prosecuted later. The plaintiffs suffered from this harm and filed this lawsuit to request the court to investigate, summon, and convict the defendant. The plaintiffs also filed a civil lawsuit to request the court to order the defendant to repay 19,566.459 taels and pay interest calculated from May 27th of the 19th year until the date of enforcement, according to the rates of Shen Bank Money Exchange and discounted money exchanges. Yesterday, Judge Feng Shide summoned the defendant, and lawyer Wu Linkun requested a postponement, which the court granted.

A Fire at Qichang Warehouse Causes a Loss of Two Million

District Chief Zhang Visited in Person to Investigate

The Fire Was Caused by a Short Circuit

The British Ewo Yoko's Qichang Warehouse H warehouse in Pudong was accidentally destroyed by a fire, burning a large number of printed fabrics and other items. This newspaper reported yesterday that the Director of the Public Security Bureau and District Chief Zhang of the Third District personally visited to investigate the cause of the fire. It was caused by a short circuit in the warehouse. In addition to the H warehouse being completely destroyed, over 8,000 bales of printed fabrics stored in the warehouse by Jiangshang Fujia, Rixin, and Dongmian Fourth Yoko were also burned. Each bale was calculated at 150 yuan, totaling a loss of 1.2 million yuan. Together with the warehouse and other goods, the total loss was nearly 2 million yuan. The warehouse had insurance of over 100,000 yuan taken out by the company, and the printed fabrics and other items were insured separately by each company, but the amounts are unknown. District Chief Zhang reported the details of the fire and the approximate losses to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for review.

雪蝶案 Judgment

Lin Xuehuai, previously dissatisfied with the first instance judgment in which Hu Die sued him for breach of engagement and recovery of debt, continued to retain lawyers Oson Ni and Ao to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Hu Die, also dissatisfied with the fact that her claim for compensation for mental distress was not fully upheld, filed a cross-appeal at the same time. The court has now concluded the hearing and rejected both appeals. Both parties are responsible for the costs of the second instance. This was previously reported. The judgment in this case has now been officially delivered to both parties. The facts and reasons are extracted as follows:

Facts: The appellant (Lin Xuehuai) declared that the original judgment should be overturned, the appellee's (Hu Die's) claims in the first instance and cross-appeal should be rejected, and the appellee should bear the costs of both instances. The appellant's statement of facts roughly stated that the breach of engagement in this case did not comply with Article 972 of the Civil Code, so there was no reason for the breach. If it is considered that the breach of engagement was initiated by the appellant, that is a mistake. The appellant's offer had already been rejected, so it had already lost its binding force, as stipulated in Article 155 of the Civil Code. Moreover, the intention to break the engagement came from the appellee, who had Zhou Jianyun invite the appellant to a conversation, at which point it was learned that the appellee had already decisively broken the engagement. This can be seen from the appellee's actions. The original trial did not examine the facts or the law, and ordered the engagement broken, which is unacceptable. The Hu Die Company was founded by the appellee's father. According to the law, the appellee's father should be the principal party. The appellee's father is still alive, and inheritance has not yet begun, so the appellee cannot exercise rights on behalf of his father. Moreover, the debts claimed, such as 380 taels for the car, 138.2 yuan for the Hardoon's apartment rent, and 50 yuan for Rong Kangxiang Western clothes, have already been repaid to the appellee. The account books were destroyed, making it impossible to audit them. The 600-yuan check from the Star Company was entrusted by the appellee to the appellant to withdraw money from the bank, which was immediately handed over to the appellee. At the time, they were engaged, so no receipt was issued. The original trial used this check, which failed to prove the debt relationship, to conclude that the debt occurred. This shows blatant bias. As for the appellant's claim for 1,000 yuan in damages, the appellant did not suffer any losses, and the cross-appeal is completely unreasonable. The appellee (Hu Die) declared that the appeal should be rejected, the cross-appellant (Hu Die) should be awarded 1,000 yuan in compensation for mental distress, and the appellant should bear the costs of both instances. The statement of facts roughly stated that the engagement was first terminated by the appellant, who twice sent letters through a lawyer requesting termination. The letters and newspaper reports falsely accused the appellee of improper conduct and a bad reputation. Moreover, his written statements already indicated that the relationship had ended. This constitutes the conditions for a major event as defined in Article 976, paragraph 9 of the Civil Code. The original judgment approving the termination of the engagement was extremely appropriate. The property of the Hu Die Company is jointly owned by the appellee and her father. The appellee's father, Hu Shaogong, testified in court, which can be verified in the original trial transcript. What the appellant said is completely fabricated and misinterprets the law. Regarding the payment of 380 taels for the car, 138.2 yuan for the Hardoon's apartment rent, and 50 yuan for Rong Kangxiang Western clothes, there are check stubs to prove it. The appellant also lacked security deposit due to gold transaction. He implored the appellee to borrow a check of 600 yuan from the Shanghai Star Film Company. After he withdrew the money himself, he turned to Shanghai Bank to deposit money in a new account. The facts are all there. The appellant knew that the appellee's company suffered a fire, and all the account books and goods were destroyed. However, he deliberately demanded the presentation of account books. Its intention is nothing more than attempting to escape the responsibility. The appeal should be rejected. As for the reason why the engagement was terminated is as stated above. The blame should be attributed to the appellant's party. According to Articles 978 and 979 of the Civil Code, the appellee requests 1,000 yuan in compensation for mental distress, which is not excessive.

Reason: The reasons for this case can be divided into three parts, which are explained separately below. (1) Regarding the engagement: The termination of the engagement was first requested by the appellant, as evidenced by the letter from the appellant to the lawyer Oson, which contains the words "the relationship has ended" and "it is unbearable" and "Please proceed with the termination of the engagement according to the law." The appellant does not dispute the contents of the letter. However, the appellant claims that the talk of breaking the engagement was expressed to Zhou Jianyun earlier, and that the appellee had already rejected the appellant's offer and lost its binding force. His claims are contradictory. Moreover, according to Zhou Jianyun's testimony in the original trial, the appellee did not express any intention to break the engagement at the beginning, and there is no proof that the appellee rejected the appellant's offer. Since the termination of the engagement was requested by the appellant first, the appellee then sued for the termination of the engagement. The original trial's judgment ordering the termination is not wrong. (2) Regarding the debt: The Hu Die Company paid 380 taels for the car, 138.2 yuan for the Hardoon's apartment rent, and 50 yuan for Rong Kangxiang Western clothes on behalf of the appellant. The appellant admits this without objection. The appellant also admits that the 600-yuan check from the Star Film Company was withdrawn by him. However, the appellant's defense is that the Hu Die Company was founded by the appellant's father, Hu Shaogong, and the appellee did not obtain Hu Shaogong's authorization, so he could not sue. The payment for the car, apartment rent, and Rong Kangxiang Western clothes has been repaid, and the check from the Star Film Company was delivered to the appellee after it was withdrawn. This court found that the Hu Die Company was jointly founded by the appellee and her father, Hu Shaogong. Hu Shaogong testified clearly in the trial and said that the lawsuit was agreed upon together. Therefore, the creditor's rights of the Hu Die Company are jointly owned by the appellee and her father. There is nothing illegal for the appellee to sue. As for the payment of various items, the appellant said that it has been repaid, but there is no way to prove it. Even if the appellee failed to produce the account books as evidence, attacking the appellant for concealing the account books, the Hu Die Company had suffered a fire. The letter from the Anping Water and Fire Insurance Company submitted by the appellant's lawyer is sufficient to prove that the appellee said that the account books were destroyed in the fire, which is not unreasonable. It cannot be said to be concealment. (3) Regarding the 600-yuan check from the Star Film Company, the appellee said that the appellant had raised 500 taels and deposited it in the Hongkou Branch of the Shanghai Commercial and Savings Bank. Although this court sent a letter to the bank to verify, it could not be confirmed. However, the check was withdrawn by the appellant and stamped with Xuehuai's chop. If the appellant does not have other evidence to prove that it has been delivered to the appellee, he cannot be exempted from the responsibility of repayment. It does not matter whether the appellant has deposited the money in Shanghai Bank. The original trial ordered the appellant to repay the above items, which is also appropriate. The above appeals cannot be said to be reasonable. Based on the above judgment, both the appeal and cross-appeal are unreasonable. According to Article 517 and Article 103 of the Civil Procedure Regulations, the judgment is as stated in the main text.

Yan Jinbiao, Sentenced to Death, Identifies Li Guocheng

Identifies Li Guocheng in a Photo of Ten People

Request to bring Li for Retrial

The Fasheng New Hostel at 113 Xinxiaoqiao Street, French Concession, on the evening of August 15 of this year, a robbery and murder case occurred in Room 2, killing Xia Yongsheng and two others surnamed Xue and Jiang Zhongfa. The French police arrested the suspect Yan Jinbiao, also known as Yan Er, from Funing, and found that Yan had committed three cases of gang robbery this spring. He was sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and sentenced to death. Yan refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the High Third Branch. The result of the trial was still a death sentence, and he was detained for execution. Now, Yan is in custody and has submitted a petition requesting the arrest of Li Guocheng, a key suspect in the case, for questioning. It is now known that Li was arrested and detained by the Public Security Bureau in the Chinese Concession for another case. The Second Special Court prepared a document and sent police to the Public Security Bureau to bring him. The Public Security Bureau replied that a total of ten people were captured in the case, and it was necessary to identify who Li was before transferring him. Therefore, the photos of the ten captured suspects were sent to the Second Special Court. At 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, Criminal Judge Ge Zhitan sat in the Criminal Court III and ordered the suspect Yan to be brought for questioning. Yan confessed that the murder case was actually committed by Li Guocheng. The people were arrested and sentenced to death. The real situation was a miscarriage of justice. He requested a clear understanding and the arrest of Li for questioning. The official showed the photos to Yan and ordered him to identify the face of the suspect Li. Yan accepted the photos and, after examining them, pointed out the second photo from the right in the second row as Li Guocheng. The official said that he must identify clearly and not rush to identify. Yan replied that he and Li were from the same village and knew each other, so he would not make a mistake, and that Li was a very famous person in the Jiangbei area. Judge Ge then ordered him to wait for a change of date to transfer Li Guocheng for questioning. Yan was still detained.

Lu Xingdi's Problem of Forcing Prostitution

Circumstances of Repeated Prostitution

Lu Xingdi, a 16-year-old woman from Jiading, because she was not yet an adult, retained lawyer Cai Jishi as her legal representative, with her mother, Lu Lu (43 years old), as her legal guardian. She filed a criminal complaint with the Second Special Court, accusing the woman Li Liu of restricting her freedom. She stated that the woman usually made a living farming in her hometown, but because she had many children and could not afford to raise them, she entrusted her daughter Xingdi to the care of Li Liu, the landlady of the Hefeng Hotel on Simalu Road, four years ago, through Chen Jinqing, to learn opera, so that she could rely on her for life in the future. Later, because the hotel was being renovated, it moved without a trace. The woman came to Shanghai several times to look for her, but still could not find her. She was in despair. Unexpectedly, last month, her daughter suddenly returned home alone, recounting the situation of being forced into prostitution by Liu. Therefore, she was unwilling to give up and filed a lawsuit, requesting an investigation. Lu Xingdi said that after she was introduced to Liu's family by Chen Jinqing, she first learned opera, and then was sent to a brothel in Hankou to work as a prostitute. Last March, she came to Shanghai and was again taken to the Aimei Brothel on Shantou Road. In May, she went to the Lijuan Brothel in Leyu Lane, and in August, she went to the Yinghong Brothel in Fuyu Lane. She has been repeatedly forced into prostitution several times and has been abused. Therefore, she could not bear the suffering and escaped back to her mother's home. This is the truth. Li Liu, who is 60 years old and from Suzhou, said that she opened the Hefeng Hotel. The daughter of the plaintiff is actually a prostitute who runs the hotel. She has never learned opera at the woman's place, and has never been forced into prostitution. She also hired a lawyer to defend her. After a long period of mutual defense by the lawyers of both parties, the presiding judge ordered the defendant to post bail and wait for a continued hearing on another date.

Woman Hu Shanshan Sues Her Brother for Living Expenses

Failed to Reach an Agreement

The woman Zai Shanshan, who is 31 years old, is a spinster. Recently, she retained lawyer Chen Tingrui to file a lawsuit with the Civil Court of the First Special District, accusing her brothers Hu Disheng and Hu Lansheng of occupying her inheritance and illegal insults, and requesting an allowance for living expenses. The complaint stated that the plaintiff was born at an unfortunate time. Seven months after she was born, her father Youxiang died of illness, leaving behind nearly one million yuan in property, which was managed by her eldest brother Disheng and second brother Lansheng. Disheng was born to the plaintiff's former mother, Zhou, and Lansheng was born to the plaintiff's biological mother, Cheng. When Youxiang passed away, the plaintiff was still an infant and had no knowledge of anything. Afterwards, time passed quickly, and the defendants treated the plaintiff as a stranger, with the power in their hands. Even the daily supply of food and clothing was met with complaints. The plaintiff complained about her bad fate and adhered to the principle of not marrying for life. Now that she is over 30 years old, she lives in Lansheng's place and is spared from freezing and starvation thanks to the protection of her biological mother. However, the defendants' cold eyes and taunts made it difficult for the plaintiff to tolerate herself. For the sake of her lifelong livelihood, she intended to ask the defendants to give her a discretionary allowance for living expenses. Therefore, this year, she entrusted lawyer Jiang Bao to send a letter on her behalf. Unexpectedly, the defendants not only did not reply or agree to give her the allowance, but instead insulted her arbitrarily and even wanted to drive the plaintiff out. The plaintiff, in her resentment, had no choice but to seek legal remedy. Considering that her father Youxiang had passed away for 30 years, according to the current Civil Code, the plaintiff has no provision to request a re-analysis of the inheritance. However, after reviewing the precedent of the Dali Court, No. 318 of the Five Years, it is stated that before a sister is married, the expenses of raising her should be borne equally by each brother and sister. There should be no discrimination based on whether they have the same mother or not. The second half of No. 669 of the Three Years states that if the biological mother is liked by her family, she should be given a share of the property without any doubt. However, the benchmark for apportionment should be based on the wishes of the parents. If the parents did not express their wishes during their lifetime, the trial court should consider the situation and the status of the estate to determine the benchmark. No. 761 of the Seven Years states that if the biological mother is liked by her family, the mother may be given a discretionary amount of the inheritance after the father's death, but it should be less than the amount divided equally among the number of people who should be divided. Now that the plaintiff is determined not to marry for life, and the defendants have an inheritance of one million yuan under their management, according to the above precedents, they have the obligation to support the plaintiff and give her a discretionary allowance for living expenses. The plaintiff's request is based on the kinship and the legal principles of the precedents. The defendants should not have refused so sternly, and even insulted and expelled her. Although the plaintiff requested the court to mediate, the defendants all denied and claimed that the inheritance was only tens of thousands of yuan, resulting in the failure of mediation. At that time when the defendants inherited the estate from their father, the will recorded the actual number. If the defendants were ordered to hand over the will for reference, it could prove that what the plaintiff said was true. Therefore, please summon the defendants and order them to jointly pay the plaintiff 100,000 yuan for living expenses and bear the costs of the lawsuit. This case has been heard by the court once, and it was ordered to try mediation. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Daren of the Civil Court held another hearing and questioned the lawyers of both parties about the mediation. However, both defendants failed to appear as summoned. According to the defendant's lawyer, his lawyer had mediated with the plaintiff's lawyer, Tingrui, but the plaintiff stated that she needed 100,000 yuan, while the defendant was willing to give 1,000 yuan. The amount was too far apart, resulting in the failure of mediation. Judge Zhou said that the two parties were siblings and it was best to mediate. He must know that litigation will eventually lead to misfortune. He persuaded both parties to compromise and not go to extremes. The defendant's lawyer then said that according to the defendant, he would give the plaintiff 30 mu of farmland in Yuyao. The land price there was quite expensive at first, about 100 yuan per mu, but now it has fallen to 70 or 80 yuan per mu. When the plaintiff Hu Shanshan heard this, she declared that she was unwilling. Then, the plaintiff's lawyer, Chen, said that when Youxiang died, he made a will, which was recorded in detail. Now, the defendant himself is not only absent, but the will is also not brought to the court, so there is no hope of mediation. The lawyer can now cite one thing: someone from the defendant's clan failed in business and suffered a huge loss, and the defendant generously helped him with 2,000 taels of silver. Now, he is only willing to give 1,000 yuan to his sibling, which is too far apart. If the defendant can give a substantial amount, the lawyer is willing to persuade the plaintiff to compromise. Judge Zhou ordered the case to be rescheduled to January 11 next year to wait for the defendant to appear in court for another hearing.

Unemployed Fellow Townsman Threatens with Letter

Three Arrested, One Escaped

Li Anfa, the owner of the Shengli Weaving Factory at No. 831 Qiwupu Road, who is from Anhui, recently received a threatening letter written by bandits, which was stuffed into the factory fence, extorting 2,000 yuan, otherwise they would shoot him to death with a pistol and set fire to the weaving machine frame. The next morning, he sent a representative to a certain place on Taopeng Road to deliver the money, and someone would come to accept it. After Li received the letter, he was extremely frightened and reported it to the Yangshupu Police Station, which sent Chinese and Western detectives to the vicinity of the place at the appointed time to wait, but there was no trace. Li thought that the letter must have been written by unemployed fellow townsmen, so he asked his fellow villager Zhang Xuechuan to investigate. The next day, Zhang and his friend Jin Changsheng, who was also from Anhui, went to the factory and told Li that the letter was written in the French Concession, and someone named Luo Bengen knew about it. He would go to investigate further. After a while, he went to Li and asked him to go to a certain place in the French Concession to talk. Li did not go because he did not have so much money. Early in the morning, Luo Bengen, Luo Lunpu, Jin, and Zhang came to Li and negotiated, asking him to pay 1,500 yuan to settle the matter. Li refused, and the amount was reduced to 1,000 yuan or 800 yuan. Li still pleaded to reduce it, and Jin and Zhang mediated, reducing it to at least 200 or 300 yuan. Seeing this situation, Li determined that this matter was done by them, so he secretly reported it to the police station, which sent detectives to arrest Luo Lunpu, Jin Changsheng, and Zhang Xuechuan, while Luo Bengen took the opportunity to escape. Yesterday, they were sent to the First Special Court Gao Yi Court. Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the police station, stated the previous situation and requested a postponement. He then presented the threatening letter for inspection. Then, Li Anfa, the victim, reported the situation, and Luo and the other three defendants were questioned. They all claimed that they were mediating the threatening letter for Li and had no accomplices. They asked for a review. Judge Shen Bingrong ordered them all to be detained and waited for a continued hearing to investigate.

Two Unfortunate Deaths in Wusong

Climbing Crabs: Kang Guilin, a 58-year-old resident of Kangjiagang, behind the Huafeng Yarn Factory in West Wusong, made a living by farming. However, after completing his agricultural work, he often took climbing crabs as a sideline. Therefore, he owned a sampan. Every year from the end of autumn to winter, Kang would moor his sampan on the Sitang River (near Taixing'an Bridge), and use several small square nets to climb and catch river crabs and sell them in Songzhao the next morning, as he had been accustomed to doing. Unexpectedly, while Guilin was climbing crabs the night before, a sudden northwest wind broke out. Guilin accidentally fell into the riverbank. Because it was late at night, no one rescued him at that time, and he tragically drowned, and no one noticed. It was not until yesterday morning that his son Zhanglin went and did not see his father's figure, so he searched nearby and found his father's body, and he knew that he had fallen into the river and died. So he salvaged the body, carried it back to Kangjiagang, and prepared a coffin for burial.

Swallowing Smoke: Zhu Yang, a resident of Li Jiazhaizi in West Wusong, who was nearly sixty years old, suffered from nervous disorder after going to visit relatives in Yangxing a few days ago. She secretly went out to buy raw opium and swallowed it secretly, and lay on the bed. Later, her son Lao Er saw that her face was pale and examined it carefully, and learned that she had swallowed raw smoke. He immediately ordered someone to carry his mother to Jiang Yisheng's Western doctor's office. After Dr. Jiang injected as much as 16 pounds of disinfectant, the poison had gone to the limbs and could not be saved. He was carried back home and died yesterday morning. Now, his sons Lao Er and Lao San have prepared a coffin for burial.
