Resembles a Worker

A man floated up in the Puzhong of the Taiping Wharf in Tilanqiao at 9:00 PM last night. The Hongkou Police Station salvaged it and sent it to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. It was already ineffective. The deceased was about 30 years old, wearing blue cloth clothes and pants, and looked like a worker. He was sent to the morgue for examination.

Lu Haogen Crushed His Right Hand and Died

Lu Haogen, a 32-year-old mud mason from Jiangyin at the Shenxin No. 6 Yarn Factory at Gaolangqiao in Yangshupu, was painting the wall in the workshop yesterday morning. He accidentally got caught in the machine, crushed his right hand, and injured his head. He was dying. Later, the fire brigade sent him to the Tongren Hospital for treatment by car. He died shortly after due to his serious injuries. The hospital reported it to the morgue, waiting for a report from the court for examination.

Robbery and Injury on Qingyun Road

Ge Hecai, a 39-year-old man from Haimen who worked at the Commercial Press at No. 37 Hongfa Lane, Qingyun Road, Zhabei, was suddenly visited by several bandits wearing blue-black cloth long shirts at 7:25 PM the night before. Two bandits knocked on the door, pretending to ask for a letter. Ge's wife, Ms. Chen, 38 years old, did not suspect anything and opened the door. The two bandits rushed into the living room. At that time, Ge had not returned home. A bandit wearing a black long shirt took out a pistol, threatening silence, and hugged Ms. Chen around the waist. Another bandit took off the gold jewelry on Ms. Chen's hand and fled to the door. The bandit hugging Ms. Chen also followed suit. When he reached the door, Ms. Chen dragged the bandit in blue clothes, shouting "Robbery!" The bandit in a hurry used the handle of a pistol to hit Ms. Chen's head, piercing a hole and bleeding profusely. Ms. Chen, in pain, let go and saw the bandit fleeing to the back door of No. 31, jumping on the platform to the open space in the west and escaping. The neighbor Zeng told the Pengpu Security Corps' Third Team duty platoon leader Hong Yunfa, who was nearby, to take a gun and rush to the scene, but the bandit had already fled far away. He then took the victim to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau and the Xibinxing Road Police Station to report the incident, and agreed to try to investigate. However, Ms. Chen's head was severely injured, her face was badly injured, and her nose was broken by the bandit. However, according to Ms. Chen, when she twisted and fought at the door, the bandit in the blue cloth long shirt was also bitten hard on the shoulder, and his clothes were torn. The bandit may also be injured. He was only able to escape because no one was at home and the neighbors did not dare to help.

Someone Sleeping and Snoring in a Trash Can

Likely Suffering from Mental Illness

Yesterday morning, in the Dongjiadu area of the Nanshi district, a man, appearing to be in his thirties and wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants, was found sleeping in a trash can placed by the roadside. He neither ate nor drank, which onlookers found strange. After waking him up, they asked why he was lying in the trash can, but he only stared blankly and remained silent. Shortly after, he turned over and resumed snoring loudly, appearing to be suffering from mental illness. The local police station prepared a letter and sent him to Puyutang (a charitable institution) for care. According to acquaintances, the man was usually fond of gambling, but unfortunately, he had lost repeatedly, sending all his family property into the "thirty-six gates" (gambling dens). After becoming depressed, he developed this mental illness, waving his arms and stamping his feet all day long, with erratic moods. Sometimes he would run wildly in the streets. Today, it was likely due to the cold weather that he slept in the trash can.

Reader's Letter

Tang Qi writes about the Disposal of Sealed Japanese Goods

Resisting Japanese goods has been ongoing for nine times now, and each time it has been criticized for being a "five-minute fad" because there is no thorough solution. My humble opinion on a thorough solution involves both fundamental and superficial measures: (1) Fundamental solution: Organize a state-run import and export trading company. In this era of industrial backwardness in our country, we cannot avoid importing bulk commodities. It is imperative to organize a state-run import and export trading company. Its branches should be distributed in various seaports and commercial cities. All purchases of foreign goods by Chinese people should be handled by the company. Individuals should not be allowed to directly order goods. Those who order from foreign firms should first register and obtain permission from the company. (In the future, if diplomatic solutions are available, all foreign firms importing goods to China for sale should also be handled by the company.) Those who do not register and obtain permission should be punished. Since the state-run import and export trading company is the central hub for commodity imports, people should not be allowed to order Japanese goods, and Japanese goods would then have no way to enter. (2) Superficial solution: Establish import and export registration offices in various ports. Before the establishment of the state-run trading company, each port should organize an import and export registration office. All people in the city who import goods from other ports must first register and obtain permission, then obtain a registration certificate. Carriers must verify that the registration certificate matches the goods before transporting them. Violators, both importers and carriers, will be subject to penalties. (The registration office will conduct inspections at any time.) Since the registration office is the review authority for all commodity imports in the city, people should not be allowed to purchase and transport Japanese goods, and Japanese goods would then have no way to enter. At the same time, a domestic goods promotion department could be established to introduce domestic goods to merchants to replace the foreign goods they want to purchase. However, the registration of import and export trade may cause inconvenience for law-abiding people. The quality of personnel in various ports may be uneven, and there may be abuses of power for personal gain, which is indeed worth considering. However, this is a superficial solution, and it should be abolished after the state-run import and export trading company is established. The establishment of the state-run import and export trading company should be limited to the shortest possible time. Since import and export registration offices have been established in various ports, Japanese goods will no longer be able to continue entering the country. The sealed Japanese goods within the country can be released and allowed to be sold freely, which will not affect the overall anti-Japanese action. These released sealed Japanese goods will be the last batch of Japanese goods. Shops and customers can buy and sell them with a clear conscience, and merchants' capital and the social economy can be restored as a result. When releasing the goods, merchants should pay 5% of the total value of the sealed goods to the state-run trading company as a fund. Nationwide, this should amount to more than ten million, which would allow the state-run import and export trading company to be established quickly, and Japanese goods will be permanently eradicated from our country.

(Reply) Using a state-run import and export trading company as a fundamental solution and import and export registration as a superficial solution to resist Japanese goods is indeed essential. However, the letter also considers whether registration will be inconvenient for merchants and whether officials can avoid abusing their power for personal gain. Even if the state-run company is established, whether corruption can be completely eliminated is also a question. Look at the current state-run enterprises; almost all of them are eroding the national economy, exploiting the people's livelihood, and enriching officials. Where can we talk about credibility? If there is really no solution, it is better to promote less. Furthermore, before formally declaring economic severance, using a state-run import and export trading company to absolutely prohibit the import of goods from a certain country may give that country an excuse because it comes from the government rather than the people.

Free Talk

National Salvation Motto

— Fang Yuwo

Gu Yanwu said: Combine the private interests of the world to form the public interest of the world. Napoleon said: Success belongs to the most persistent.

The ancient text "Discourses of the States" says: Brothers who slander and insult others will be exiled a hundred miles away.

A Greek proverb says: Do not take small things lightly, for they can lead to great achievements.

Peter the Great said: In times of war, do what you do in times of peace; in times of peace, do what you do in times of war.

Feng Zhuo'an said: In planning for the country, use the wisdom of the masses; in conducting oneself, rely on solitude.

Fan Chunren said: A gentleman cannot defeat a petty person in a battle of strength; only wisdom can be relied upon.

Lü Jingye said: Never let others do the most important things.

Han Tuizhi said: Rather than having praise in front, it is better to have no slander behind.

Removing Garden State's Talk Collection

Reading Chairman Ma Zhanshan's Telegram

Some time ago, Chairman Ma Zhanshan sent a telegram advising the Youth Volunteer Corps to Aid Ma in Resistance Against Japan not to go to Heilongjiang. The telegram contained these words: "...Handmaidens weave, slaves till the land, each with their own specific duties; safeguarding the country and resisting foreign aggression is the responsibility of soldiers..." Reading these words, I had two thoughts: one was a reluctance to criticize, and the other was a necessity to criticize. Why the reluctance to criticize? Chairman Ma is fighting the Japanese in the frozen wilderness, fighting for the nation's dignity amid the risk of death. His loyalty is admired by all. Even if he said a wrong word or two, the people should forgive him. How could I dare to nitpick? Why the necessity to criticize? Chairman Ma is now a universally respected figure in the country. People have almost blind faith in his words and actions. If the people, because of their admiration for Chairman Ma's merits, also regard these words as golden rules, wouldn't we all become like ancient people? I began with a reluctance to criticize, but ultimately felt compelled to criticize precisely because of this reason.

The era of handmaidens weaving and slaves tilling the land is long gone. Today, it is workers who weave cloth, not handmaidens. Today, it is farmers who till the land, not slaves. Above workers and farmers, there should no longer be those scholars who "do not toil with their limbs and cannot distinguish the five grains." The "idiot ruler" that Mr. Sun Yat-sen spoke of is not Sun Ke but our workers and farmers. Workers and farmers are the masters of the Republic of China. We should acknowledge them as masters. To treat everyone as slaves is, to put it lightly, an ideological error; to put it harshly, all acts of treason against the Republic of China by warlords throughout history originated from this single misconception. Gu Tinglin said: "The rise and fall of the world is the responsibility of every individual." Modern citizens have the duty to serve in the military, thus bearing the shared responsibility of safeguarding the country and resisting foreign aggression. The responsibility of soldiers lies not in defending the land alone but in forging the people to have the collective strength to defend the nation. If Chairman Ma can realize this idea, not only can Heilongjiang province be secured, but the entire nation will be inspired, and the Republic of China will become an impregnable land, impossible for anyone to invade.

Some say that this telegram might have been drafted by a secretary and sent without Chairman Ma's review. I say that even if Chairman Ma wrote it himself, it is a gentleman's error, like a solar eclipse, not harming his brilliance.

Wu Changqing's Foresight

— Qing Song Jushi

Japan, as an Eastern island nation, looks down on our country. Its iron cavalry roams rampant, trampling the Northeast. Although commentators say that the policy of non-resistance led to the滔天之禍 (immense disaster), they do not know that the disaster did not originate on the day of its occurrence; it must have been foreshadowed. Therefore, tracing the origin of the disaster, it almost began with the Sino-Japanese War of 1894. However, ten years before the war, among the senior generals of the Qing Dynasty, there was someone who exposed their conspiracy and wanted to prepare for a rainy day. Although I entered the world late, I heard from the elders that there was a man named Wu, who had great foresight and ambition to counter Japan. Although he died with unfulfilled aspirations, his earnest warnings about the future, saying what no one dared to say at the time, were praised by later generations. Therefore, I am following Xu Zi's example of not being afraid of bothering people and providing some assistance to those who are concerned about national affairs.

Wu's given name was Changqing, and he was given the posthumous title of Zhuang. He was from Lujiang, Anhui. He had great ambitions from a young age and studied military strategy diligently. In the early years of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty, Li Hongzhang was training troops in Suzhou and Shanghai. Wu served under his command. Although he fought in numerous eastern and western campaigns, rising to the rank of general, he did not wish to see frequent internal conflicts that harmed his own people. He was only forced to do so under overwhelming pressure, and although he did not speak of it, he felt guilty at heart. Later, in the eighth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, Wu became the admiral of the Guangdong Navy. At that time, Korean rebels attacked the Japanese embassy and affected the royal palace. The Japanese were in an uproar, thinking that they had an opportunity to take advantage of. Li Hongzhang then ordered Wu to rush to support. Upon hearing the news, Wu immediately got up, thinking that this was an opportunity to achieve merit in a foreign land and boost our national prestige. He led 5,000 soldiers and sailed swiftly by sea. By the time the Japanese soldiers arrived in Hanseong, Wu had already arrived two days earlier and was strictly on guard. The Japanese soldiers were surprised and looked at each other in shock. Wu then detected the whereabouts of the rebels, captured and beheaded dozens of people, and the matter was settled. However, the Japanese were so angry that they insisted on fabricating events. The Japanese admiral, Habusa, led troops to surround the Korean royal palace, spying on the Wu army. Scouts were sent out everywhere, spreading rumors, intending to provoke a conflict with our army. Wu had already discerned their deceitful scheme, reorganized his troops, and made the spears and halberds stern and inviolable. The Japanese were intimidated and dared not challenge. They warned each other, "Don't say they have no one; be careful not to cause trouble." After a month, Korea was largely pacified. He requested to leave five battalions to protect the area. The Koreans were grateful to him and built a shrine for him. In the following year, the tenth year of the Guangxu reign, he returned to Beijing due to illness. Knowing that he would not recover, he repeatedly told Li, "Korea's government is corrupt and the people are poor. The country is militarily weak and strategically important. The Japanese are cunning and malicious. They are eyeing Korea like tigers. It is necessary to train troops and defend it, to prevent the Eastern Japanese from causing trouble, so that Korea will forever remain a vassal state. Otherwise, the Japanese will act recklessly and inevitably annex it, and our country's barrier will be removed." His far-sighted words were like torches. The future Japanese would be like boars and long snakes, gradually feeding on the upper state. Wu was fully aware and considered it all. If Heaven had granted him more years, even if there had been the Sino-Japanese War of 1894, if he had been able to go to support, we would not have lost troops and territory, paid reparations, and been forced into a situation where we are being threatened today. The poem says, "When a good man is gone, my heart is filled with sorrow." That is why I am angry at the unrighteous Eastern Japanese and remember the stories passed down by the elders, and I admire Wu's foresight, which is beyond my reach.

World Anecdotes

A young Englishman named Gill from Whitney, England, who had worked in more than twenty different occupations, at the age of thirty-two. There are countless young people in the world.

I'm afraid no one can compare to him. He has been a newsboy, a butcher's assistant, a barber's assistant, a grocer's assistant, a telegram deliverer, a sailor on a fishing boat, a woodcarver, an electrician, a motor engineer, a chauffeur, a bricklayer, a carpenter, a cart driver, a servant, a bartender, a gardener, a radio salesman, an elevator operator, a painter, a postman, a woodcutter, and a machine foreman. He has also opened a power plant and an automobile shop, and he has traveled around the world on a simple motorized bicycle. But seeing him, at the age of thirty-two, having done so many different occupations, although he may lack perseverance, his physical health, mental agility, and ambition are evident. Moreover, it is commendable that he traveled around the world on a motorized bicycle.

Change New Year's Greeting Cards to Warning-of-the-Year Cards

— Jun Shuo

The national crisis has not ended, and the national worries have not subsided. Enthusiastic people are afraid that all sectors will follow the old practice of sending New Year's greeting cards, causing them to forget the current worries and disregard the country's great shame and humiliation. Therefore, they have advocated stopping New Year's greetings, and their views have been repeatedly disclosed in newspapers, and are known to readers. Yesterday, when the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in my hometown held a meeting, there was a proposal to go a step further than stopping New Year's greetings, saying that simply stopping greetings is still too weak. After all, many people don't send New Year's greeting cards anyway. But simply ceasing these actions does little to communicate the shock and gravity of the current moment. It would be better to change the New Year's greeting cards to "warning-of-the-year" cards. Since the beginning of the twenty-first year has nothing to celebrate and is full of disasters to be wary of, the wording on the card should be very different from before. This proposal was unanimously adopted at the time, and the words on the card were drafted as follows: "The twenty-first year has arrived. It is unbearable to look back. Great disasters lie ahead. No play, no feasting, no indulgence in the New Year. The country is on the verge of collapse. Let us encourage each other to renew and refresh ourselves. Use today's warning to leave for the celebrations of future years." So-and-so bowing with tears. I heard the description of a friend who was at the meeting like this, and I deeply agreed. If we can always maintain this concern and vigilance and use it to influence all sectors, there may be hope for our country's future. In the past, King Zhuang of Chu discussed and trained the people every day, and thus became the hegemon of the Central Plains. King Fucha of Wu, because his father Helü died in battle with Yue, had people stand in the courtyard every day. Every time he went in and out, they would call out, "Fucha, have you forgotten that the King of Yue killed your father?" Then he would answer, "No, I dare not forget." After three years, he avenged Yue. Therefore, those who have the ambition to save the country and avenge shame must have their plans constantly in place. Changing New Year's greetings to "warning-of-the-year" is deeply meaningful.

Four Casual Notes

— Shi Tianlai

The origin of the name "Shanghai": Shanghai seems to have initially been a fishing village, a place for ships to stop and dock. Its later development into a major port was based on this. The current name means "above the sea." At that time, there was also a "Lower Shanghai," perhaps because there were two seaports, hence the division into upper and lower. The place located above the sea was named "Shanghai."

The origin of "Kaisar Road": According to legend, a certain Portuguese gentleman happened to be passing by the Hongkou Circus. He heard a woman crying sadly in a tent. He redeemed her and sent her to be raised by a certain American missionary. Later, with the help of the gentleman, the woman went to the United States to study. After returning to China, she married the gentleman. Her name was Kaisar, so he jokingly called the place where she lived "Kaisar Road," meaning "the place of Kaisar." Later generations also called the place Kaisar Road.

The origin of "Foreigner Park": This place is where the Huangpu River and the Suzhou Creek converge. It was formed by silt. In the past, a ship sank here, so the silt accumulated even more. The land originally belonged to the British Consulate. Later, with the consent of the British government, it was transferred to the Public Works Department, which opened a park. Therefore, a large sum of money was spent to fill the land, and today's beautiful park emerged from a wasteland.

The name of "Bowling Alley": The origin of the name cannot be verified now, but it is known that it was located somewhere at the corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road (formerly No. 49 Nanjing Road). There was a Chinese-style house there, and a small door on the side of the house led to the bowling alley. Although the house has been rebuilt, the local people still call the place the Bowling Alley.

An Account of Returning Home Amidst the National Crisis

— Gao Yahun

The foreign invasion is intensifying, and the country is on the verge of collapse. My mind is filled with the tragic scenes of national destruction, and I have no time to think of my hometown. A few days ago, I went to Hangzhou on business and met with Mr. Chen, the director of the Photographic Team, to discuss matters. I had half a day of free time, and I could have enjoyed the scenery of the lake and mountains. However, I had little interest, and I returned to my hometown at the persuasion of a friend. Although it was only a short trip, I saw and heard many interesting things on the way, which I recorded to bring a smile to my face amidst the tears.

One River, Two Crossings: My home is in Shaoxing. Originally, one could cross the Qiantang River directly to the Xixing shore. This time, when crossing the river to the other side, I had to cross another strip of water. I couldn't help but exclaim in surprise. I asked the boatman, and he told me that a strip of sand rose in the middle of the river. During shallow tidal floods, it protruded from the water surface, so one had to cross the river twice. However, a group of coolies took this opportunity to make a lot of money.

Manpower Automobile: Although there are good and fast long-distance buses in the Shaoxing Highway Bureau, there are also many old and dilapidated ones used to make up the numbers. When the car I was riding started, it had to be pulled by dozens of coolies for half a mile before it could drive smoothly. After stopping at the station, it had to be pushed by manpower again. I couldn't name it, so I called it the "Manpower Automobile."

The Japanese Won't Come: After I arrived home, my neighbor, Mr. Wang, came to inquire about the current situation. I told him about the violent Japanese seizing our land and the impending demise of the country. Those who heard it were all furious. However, Mr. Wang seemed to disbelieve it, saying, "It's hard to believe. There's a saying: 'If you hit them, they'll come; if you scold them, they'll come; but they'll never come if it costs them money.' Would the Japanese dare to come?" It was laughable that he mistook "costing money" for "Japanese."

Begging with Kowtows: When I returned to Hangzhou after spending the night at home, I saw dozens of students begging for donations in Jianggan. When they encountered an old villager who didn't open his purse, the students surrounded the old villager and kowtowed. The old villager was forced to search his purse for a long time and took out a two-cent coin, threw it on the ground, and fled. The onlookers all burst into laughter.

Eagle and Rabbit United: After I arrived in Hangzhou, Mr. Chen of the Photographic Team, because the filming of "Female Knight of the Barren River" was about to be completed, asked me to take an eagle and a rabbit back to Shanghai first. The eagle and rabbit were placed in a basket, and I originally wanted them to unite, but when the eagle saw the rabbit, it wanted to peck at it, and the rabbit was frightened and jumped wildly. So, they were placed in separate places. When boarding the car, I placed the eagle on the luggage rack and the rabbit under the seat. Only then were they at peace.

Fully Tasting Eagle Droppings: One passenger saw that there were few people and lay down on the car seat. Before he knew it, the droppings of the white eagle in the basket on the luggage rack dripped straight down through the gaps in the board, right on the face of the sleeping passenger. The passenger got up and argued with me. I repeatedly apologized, and it finally stopped.

Brief News: The National Salvation Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition, organized by Ms. He Xiangning, is scheduled to open on the 28th. It features over 700 selected works by more than 60 calligraphers and painters. Calligraphers and painters will be invited to collaborate on the spot. It is also heard that Mr. Hu Wenhu, the owner of Yong'an Hall, will donate two airplanes to the association for rescue purposes.

Records of What I Saw and Heard in the Old Capital

— Zhu An

Courtyard Houses

Professor Wang Guowei of Haining once wrote a book, "A Comprehensive Study of the Mingtang Temple and Burial Chamber." According to the oracle bone script, the common architectural system in ancient times was four palaces facing each other with a courtyard in the middle. The courtyard was the central space. The "Book of Rites" says that the head of the family is in the central hall, and the lord of the country is at the altar of the soil and grain, which means that the central space of a family is a place for gatherings. If we follow the old saying that the central space was a leaky place for cave dwellings, it would be contrary to reason and difficult to understand. With this theory established, all the ritual systems of the Mingtang Temple and Burial Chamber, which have been disputed by ancient and modern classical masters, can be clearly explained and proven. Wang was the chief scholar of modern Chinese studies. He was a man of faith, fond of learning, and purely Confucian. He was also proficient in European writing, knowledgeable in the arts, and able to use Western scientific methods to organize ancient traditions. Every time he established a theory, it resonated with people's hearts. Not only were the old people who stubbornly adhered to tradition unable to catch up with him, but even contemporary scholars, who held different views, had to admit his profound knowledge. Wang drowned himself in Kunming Lake in the Summer Palace in the summer of 1927 because he was indignant about the current situation. The academic circles of the whole country lost a guiding star. However, his posthumous writings were even more valued by the world. "The Interpretation of the Classics" is Wang's most brilliant work in explaining the classics. Using it to verify the common architectural style of the Northern Capital, it is almost unshakable. Most middle-class families in the Northern Capital have courtyard houses, with three or five rooms in the main house, three rooms each in the east and west wing rooms, and three or five rooms in the living room facing the main house, which the Northerners call the "inverted seat." This is exactly in line with Wang's theory of four palaces facing each other. The customs of the north mostly follow the ancient ways. Today, cave dwellings still exist in Shanxi and Shaanxi, so there is no doubt that the ancient palace system exists in the Northern Capital. Moreover, the palaces also largely follow the ancient system. The residents of the capital have a fixed style, which is just a microcosm of the palaces. To put it bluntly, Northern architecture is sufficient to represent ancient architecture.

Generally, the gate of a residence cannot face the central hall directly. It must be opened on the right side. Only public offices and royal residences have vermilion gates and latticed windows, with hitching posts in front. Royal residences also have halberds. The heavy gates are wide open and can lead directly to the inner chambers. All other civilian residences open the right door. There is a study inside the gate (a small room next to the gate), which is commonly called the gatehouse and is where the servants live. Connected to the gatehouse is the "inverted seat" mentioned above. Guests enter it. Next to it may be a small courtyard, which can be used as a kitchen and privy. The inverted seat and the main house must be separated by a short wall and a screen door, commonly called a "hanging flower door," because its short pillars are carved into the shape of inverted lotus buds. Entering the hanging flower door is the courtyard of the main house, which is where the main house and wing rooms mentioned above are located. Generally, the main house is where one sleeps and lives, while the wing rooms are used as studies, guesthouses, or to house children and store miscellaneous items. Behind the main house, there may be a small courtyard, called the "back light room." Next to it, there may be another separate courtyard, which may be used to house servants and maids. Only families above the middle class can afford this. In short, most of the houses in the capital are of the above-mentioned courtyard style. Even if there are thousands of changes, they are only remarkable for their corridors and interconnected rooms. The general structure does not deviate from this. Lower than that, there is the three-sided style, which means there is no inverted seat. If it is a poor family's residence, it is a miscellaneous courtyard, unable to have this style.

Social News

1931 Nobel Prize in Chemistry Winner: Wang Fengren

According to a dispatch from Berlin, since Alfred Nobel first initiated the prize in 1901, the Swedish Academy of Sciences has consistently favored scientists engaged in general theoretical work when selecting recipients. However, this year, this custom has been altered. The prize for this year will be shared by two renowned German scientists: Dr. Friedrich Bergius and Dr. Karl Bosch. They have not only achieved worldwide recognition for their theoretical scientific research but have also demonstrated practical effectiveness in the methods they have developed and perfected. Therefore, within the esteemed scientific community, this is considered a rare historical event.

(1) Dr. Bergius

He was interviewed at the Adlon Hotel in Berlin by representatives of a certain news agency. He was described as a cheerful, robust man, well-dressed, and just turning forty-seven this year. He expressed a sense of gratitude and joy upon receiving this prestigious award. Congratulatory gifts arrived like snowflakes, transforming his suite into a flower shop.

Regarding his chemical research, he stated that it was limited to coal and wood. He initially studied chemistry under the guidance of Professor Haber (a previous Nobel Prize winner), who drew his attention specifically to natural products. Later, in 1901, he began researching the most efficient and economical ways to utilize these raw materials. Subsequently, after painstaking efforts and sometimes sacrificing significant expenses for experimentation, he encountered several disappointments and setbacks before finally achieving success and reaching his goal: extracting oil from coal. When he announced his practical invention, his fame spread rapidly. The most important aspect of this invention is that the ratio of carbon to gas in raw coal is 1:16, while in coal oil, their ratio is 1:8. In other words, liquid fuel (oil) contains twice the amount of light gas, making its efficiency greater than that of raw coal. Therefore, it is now utilized in various industries worldwide, especially in various driving engines, where it is an indispensable component. However, when we look back at the global supply of coal oil, it is ultimately finite. Wouldn't that create a coal oil panic? On the other hand, countries like Germany, England, China, and Japan have abundant coal reserves but virtually no coal oil production. Therefore, they can now utilize Dr. Bergius's method to extract coal oil from large coal deposits, supply their domestic consumption, and become oil-independent nations. In that case, the coal oil panic would be postponed for at least tens of millions of years.

However, Dr. Bergius is not limited to researching the method of extracting oil from coal. He believes that there are other valuable substances in wood that are worth studying. Therefore, after another round of laborious research, he invented another method. Using this method, carbohydrates can be produced from wood. Now, take an example: if cellulose in any plant is strongly decomposed using hydrochloric acid under certain conditions, the result becomes sugar. Dr. Bergius's invention of this method is a significant contribution to industry.

Now, wood can be transformed into other valuable substances. For example, using Dr. Bergius's method, two-thirds of a piece of wood can be converted into carbohydrates. These can be dissolved in water and used as animal feed. With further modification, they can also be used as human food. The remaining one-third becomes various by-products, such as acetic acid and lignite. This lignite can still be processed into charcoal like ordinary wood.

Dr. Bergius's invention enables the effective utilization of wood and generates greater profits. Therefore, various countries around the world will inevitably follow suit sooner or later. This is an expected outcome. Taking Germany as an example, it imports no less than three million tons of animal feed annually, and it has been trying to plug this leak, but without a suitable solution. Recently, after Dr. Bergius invented this method, it will soon be put into practice. As for other countries rich in forests, they can naturally convert wood into alcohol and other materials for effective use in the near future.

(2) Dr. Karl Bosch

He is the nephew of Karl Bosch, a renowned electrical engineer. He is 57 years old this year. In addition to serving as the general manager of the German Chemical Trust, he has also been elected as a director of the Nobel (i.e., the initiator of the prize) Company. Therefore, he is not only a renowned scientist and chemical engineer but also one of the leading figures in the German business community.

His fame worldwide dates back to when Professor Haber won the Nobel Prize. Because Professor Haber's initial invention of extracting gas from the air could not have been successful without Dr. Bosch's assistance and the construction of a necessary machine to complete the final steps. Dr. Bosch has created a special artistic term in chemistry, which is that he can produce light gas at 750 degrees Fahrenheit and under 200 degrees of air pressure. The tangible result of Dr. Bosch's efforts is that the German Chemical Trust in Leuna and Oppau has several large machines that can produce a large amount of fertilizer, not only eliminating the need for imports from Chile but also exceeding domestic needs.

During the European War, Germany's need for gas for processing explosives and fertilizers disrupted the normal supply. If there had been no Haber-Bosch method, the country would have inevitably lacked these two items, and the war might not have lasted until November 1918.

Since the first Nobel Prize was awarded in 1901, the Chemistry Prize has been awarded 27 times. Germans have won the most, 15 times, followed by the United Kingdom with 5 times, then France and Sweden with 3 times each, and Switzerland, the United States, and Czechoslovakia with 1 time each.

### Eça de Queirós's Last Work to Be Published

Eça de Queirós, the famous Portuguese realist novelist, is said to have his last work published soon for the world to see. This manuscript was found by the late writer's children in old trunks. It includes a large collection of unpublished and only partially published manuscripts. The first to be published is a novel, translated into Spanish by W. Fernandez and titled La Capital. Three more will be published consecutively.

Recent News from the New York Publishing World: Anping

Dodd, Mead & Co. has recently published a very interesting book with a rather novel format, compiled by Mr. Sweethouse, titled "Ten Great Women of America." These ten women are all very famous in the United States. This book completely records the life histories of these ten people. The selection of these ten people was not easy. The ten are Theodosia Burr, Gana Addams, Emily Dickinson, Lucia Zora, Helen Keller, Cecilia Beaux, Mande Adams, Nancy Astor, Geraldine Farrar, and Sakajowea. The last one is said to be a Native American.

(3) Photographs are acceptable if they feature youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama performances, lectures, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. Both individuals and groups are welcome. Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

Youth Garden

The Question of Washing One's Face

— Bing

During Chinese class this afternoon, inexplicably, the Discipline Office repeatedly called out male and female students one after another. This drew the attention of the entire class, causing surprise and unease. The atmosphere became tense, and even the teacher felt strange. So, he put down the textbook and asked the students seriously, "What's going on in this class? Why is the Discipline Office calling you out one after another?"

Everyone said in unison, "We don't know."

"You don't know? You wouldn't not know what's happening in your own class. Would the Discipline Office call you out one after another if nothing happened? Others might not know, but the people who were called out must know, right?"

But everyone remained silent. The students who had been called to the Discipline Office also said, "Nothing happened."

"Humph," the teacher said helplessly, "Next time, pay attention to yourselves, follow the rules and regulations, and don't let the Discipline Office call you out during class again, especially during my class. I won't let you go out if you're called out again, but if you're found to have violated the rules, you will be severely punished."

In this mysterious and tense atmosphere, an hour passed imperceptibly. As soon as the bell rang to end the class, the classroom became chaotic. Everyone asked the students who had gone to the Discipline Office why they were "eating big dishes."

At this time, I heard the words "eating big dishes" and didn't understand what they meant. So, I asked a classmate beside me what "eating big dishes" meant.

He said, "You don't even know what eating big dishes means?"

I said, "I don't."

He said, "Eating big dishes means going to the Discipline Office."

Oh, I suddenly understood. At the same time, driven by curiosity, I eagerly wanted to know why they were "eating big dishes." So, I joined their group to find out what was going on.

The result of asking still didn't make me very clear, but I knew it was roughly about the matter of male and female students (what happened yesterday afternoon). This further piqued my interest. I must find out what's going on.

I ran to the dormitory to find Juan because she was also part of it and must know the whole story.

Juan stood angrily by the window. I pulled her and asked her to tell me what happened.

She said, "You don't know? You're asking me?"

I said, "I don't know because I asked for leave yesterday afternoon and didn't come to class, so I don't know anything at all."

She said, "Oh, that's right. You weren't in class yesterday afternoon. Ah, Bing, we were so angry yesterday. Xin was so angry that she cried in class."

Huang Shan, Director of Discipline at the Patriotic Girls' School

I was stunned and asked, "Why did she cry? Crying in class? I think the male students must have laughed at us. Girls only know how to cry. If there's anything, just negotiate with him. Why cry in class?"

Juan said, "This matter made her too embarrassed. No wonder she was so angry that she cried. I was so angry that I wanted to die. The male students insulted the dignity and personality of us female students. And not just this time, we've often been bullied by them before. You always know. This time, although Xin wasn't good at first, they bullied us too much. If we don't give them a warning this time, we'll be despised by them even more next time."

The cause of the matter was like this: Yesterday afternoon, after the second lesson of ethics, Xin, Ying, and a few others were joking around. Just as a student from another area passed by Xin, he bumped into Xin. When she saw this student's face, she laughed and said to me, "This person is so lazy, I'm afraid he didn't even wash his face today."

"Who knew he would hear it. 'Yes, I didn't even wash my waist today. I don't need anyone to love me. Unlike you female students, who are beautiful, washing your faces dozens of times a day and applying hundreds of times of powder and rouge, so beautiful...' There were also all kinds of unbearable words. I couldn't listen anymore, so I said, 'Watch your words, don't talk nonsense and insult people arbitrarily.' Xin was so angry that she couldn't say a word. Other classmates (who Xin usually doesn't pay much attention to) took this opportunity to take revenge. They attacked from several sides. I had no choice but to tell Xin not to pay attention to them and pulled her out of the classroom. She said angrily that she didn't want to study here anymore and be angry with these barbaric classmates."

When the third lesson of philology started, I went into the classroom first, and Xin came in later. As soon as she entered the classroom, the male students made a strange noise and wrote words insulting her personality on the blackboard and on her desk. So, she cried angrily. We were also angry on her behalf. Their behavior was not only insulting to her alone, but it can be said that it insulted all of us. So, we were no longer polite to them and ran to the Discipline Office to ask the Discipline teacher, 'Are we here to study or to be joked with and bullied by male students?' and asked him to go to the classroom himself to see the words on the blackboard and the desk, and whether female students should be joked with by male students."

"The Discipline Office was also very angry when they saw this classroom disturbance. They said they would investigate and punish those who did it severely. The students who were called out today are either suspects or were called out to ask questions."

The result of "eating big dishes" this time was that several male students received a major demerit, and the female students were taught a few sentences, saying that they should not talk to male students too much in class, and should not laugh at them. "You also have some fault in this matter." After listening to Juan's words, I finally understood the details of this storm, but I didn't expect that the trigger of this incident was originally just a matter of washing one's waist.

Shanghai Market

Business News

The Chinese Merchants Advertising Company announced that the Ford Motor Company's Roush plant in Dearborn, Michigan, is currently renovating all its electric engines. The 27,000 engines range in size from small enough to operate a sewing machine to large enough to generate 1,750 horsepower. The entire project is now 45% complete. The expenditure has exceeded 6 million gold dollars. It will take approximately two more years to complete the installation. This project is extremely large, requiring the factory's DC engines to be converted to AC engines. This move is part of the company's expansion plan to meet future needs. After the renovation, engine consumption can be reduced, workers can work more safely, and production equipment can be easily expanded. In the beginning, Ford engineers studied the entire plant's equipment in detail. The dimensions and tasks of all old-fashioned engines were taken into consideration. After the research, a list was made, and the needs of each factory building and each part were listed one by one. All machines, from small parts to one-mile-long vehicles, were affected. It has now been proven that each machine can save one to two horsepower after this reinstallation. The current completed equipment can save a total of more than 2,000 horsepower compared to the previous equipment. The Lincoln Motor Company, a part of the Ford Motor Company, will also be renovated at its Detroit plant, estimated to cost approximately US$600,000.

The Liangchen Hao You Society at the intersection of Beijing Road and Zhejiang Road announced that the company has new samples of stationery, envelopes, business cards, and New Year's cards, each with 60 to 70 pieces, for selection or custom printing. There are more than a hundred kinds of paper materials, fonts, drawings, and formats. A sample can be obtained for a fee of one dime. There are also special benefits. The samples are limited to 10,000 copies.

Publishing News

The Chinese Electrical Engineering Journal Society of the College of Engineering of Zhejiang University in Hangzhou announced that the "Electrical Engineering" journal issued by the society has been published for two years. Due to its valuable engineering content, it has been well received by colleagues in the electrical industry. The sales volume has been increasing recently, and it has been published to Volume 2, Issue 5. The sixth issue of Volume 2 is scheduled to be published at the end of the year. The content is unusually rich, including Bao Guobao's design of the new power plant of the Capital Power Plant, Zhao Zengjue's radio link for wired telephone, Gu Yuxiu's graphical solution of cubic equations, Wang Chongzhi's overview of Soviet electrification, etc. The price is still 30 cents per copy, and the postage is 4 cents. For the sake of preferential treatment for annual subscribers, all six issues for the whole year will be charged only 1.5 yuan, plus postage. Those who wish to subscribe can write directly to the Society.
